docs/research/ndk/wot-and-sessions.md:145:- **The session "one long-lived sub per active user, closeOnEose: false, kinds: [3, 10000, 10001, 10002]" pattern IS the framework-magic core for kind:3 auto-tracking.** NMP's session module owns this subscription; UI components never see it; the kernel publishes "follows changed" deltas to any view that declared interest in "current account's follows".
docs/research/ndk/missing-features-for-nmp.md:3:What NDK provides, what NMP M2 needs, and the delta.
docs/research/ndk/missing-features-for-nmp.md:12:- Core NDK: filters are immutable post-`subscribe()`. There is no follow-list watcher. The closest mechanism (`outboxTracker.on("user:relay-list-updated", …) → refreshRelayConnections`) only adds *relays*, not *authors*.
docs/research/ndk/missing-features-for-nmp.md:19:- Either way: this is at least one file (~200 LOC) of NMP-specific glue per platform — AND the framework-magic contract (`docs/design/framework-magic.md`) must promise the app dispatches zero code while the kernel does the stop/restart on kind:3 arrival.
docs/research/ndk/missing-features-for-nmp.md:32:### 3. No persisted outbox tracker
docs/research/ndk/missing-features-for-nmp.md:34:`OutboxTracker.data` is an in-memory LRU (`core/src/outbox/tracker.ts:62-65`). On every cold app start, NDK re-fetches relay lists for every author the user cares about. For mobile NMP, this is a cold-start cost ~= 1 round-trip to outbox relays per ~400 authors.
docs/research/ndk/missing-features-for-nmp.md:36:Source explicitly notes the gap: `// TODO: The state of this tracker needs to be added to cache adapters` (`tracker.ts:48-49`).
docs/research/ndk/missing-features-for-nmp.md:39:- Persist `OutboxItem` data per-author in its cache (alongside kind 10002 events themselves).
docs/research/ndk/missing-features-for-nmp.md:42:## Other notable gaps for NMP M2
docs/research/ndk/missing-features-for-nmp.md:78:`NDKSync.sync` / `syncAndSubscribe` are not the default path. Regular `ndk.subscribe` doesn't try negentropy. For large historical fetches (e.g., loading the last week of a 500-follow feed cold), NMP should reach for sync directly.
docs/research/ndk/missing-features-for-nmp.md:86:When the outbox model picks 2 relays per author, those 2 may both be slow. No automatic fallback or expansion mid-stream. NMP could add: monitor per-relay event-arrival rate; if below threshold for a given author, expand to N=3.
docs/research/ndk/missing-features-for-nmp.md:90:- Per-subscription dedup (correct cache-less).
docs/research/ndk/outbox.md:3:Primary refs: `core/src/outbox/`, `core/src/relay/sets/calculate.ts`, `core/src/ndk/index.ts`, `core/src/utils/get-users-relay-list.ts`.
docs/research/ndk/outbox.md:7:NDK implements outbox/gossip routing per NIP-65: each user advertises read/write relays (kind 10002, fallback to kind 3 content), and clients address queries to the relays where each author actually publishes — not to a fixed soup of "popular" relays.
docs/research/ndk/outbox.md:11:1. **`OutboxTracker`** (`core/src/outbox/tracker.ts`) — LRU-cached map `pubkey → OutboxItem { readRelays, writeRelays, relayUrlScores }`. Fetches relay lists in batches of 400, emits `user:relay-list-updated` when a list arrives.
docs/research/ndk/outbox.md:13:3. **`chooseRelayCombinationForPubkeys`** (`core/src/outbox/index.ts:45`) — given N pubkeys + a per-author goal (default 2 relays each), picks the minimum relay set that covers every author. Prefers already-connected relays, then pool-permanent relays, then sorted by relay ranking.
docs/research/ndk/outbox.md:20:    this.outboxPool = new NDKPool(opts.outboxRelayUrls || DEFAULT_OUTBOX_RELAYS, ...);
docs/research/ndk/outbox.md:21:    this.outboxTracker = new OutboxTracker(this);
docs/research/ndk/outbox.md:24:A separate `NDKPool` is used for relay-list lookups so metadata fetches don't pollute the main read pool. Configured by `outboxRelayUrls` constructor opt; otherwise `DEFAULT_OUTBOX_RELAYS`. Disabled wholesale with `enableOutboxModel: false`.
docs/research/ndk/outbox.md:32:if (this.outboxPool && subscription.hasAuthorsFilter()) {
docs/research/ndk/outbox.md:36:    this.outboxTracker?.trackUsers(authors);
docs/research/ndk/outbox.md:41:- Skips pubkeys already in the LRU cache (placeholder set immediately to prevent duplicate in-flight fetches).
docs/research/ndk/outbox.md:42:- Calls `getRelayListForUsers()` which subscribes to `{ kinds: [10002, 3], authors }` on the outbox pool.
docs/research/ndk/outbox.md:52:this.outboxTracker.on("user:relay-list-updated", (pubkey, _outboxItem) => {
docs/research/ndk/outbox.md:66:## Write-side outbox
docs/research/ndk/outbox.md:98:Outbox tracker state is *not* persisted to cache adapters — there is a `TODO` in `tracker.ts:48-49` noting rehydration is unimplemented. On every fresh app boot, the tracker is empty and the first wave of subscriptions pays full discovery cost.
docs/research/applesauce/event-store-query-builders.md:8:There is no special path for kind:3. The kind:3 / outbox / profile reactivity that makes Applesauce feel magical is **emergent from four generic mechanisms composing**, all hooked to `EventStore.insert$` / `update$` / `remove$`:
docs/research/applesauce/event-store-query-builders.md:12:3. Refcount-based event "claims" (separate from RxJS refcounts) so the LRU pruner cannot evict events still bound to live UI.
docs/research/applesauce/event-store-query-builders.md:15:NMP must reproduce all four. Skipping any one yields either leaks, thrashing, or a broken outbox model on follow/unfollow.
docs/research/applesauce/event-store-query-builders.md:21:- a separate `EventMemory` instance used as a singleton-instance cache (`event-store.ts:111` — when a real DB is set, memory is created in addition to it),
docs/research/applesauce/event-store-query-builders.md:27:The `mapToMemory()` helper (`event-store.ts:136-142`) is the **single-instance invariant enforcer**: every event returned from the database is normalized through `EventMemory.add()` so that two reads of the same id return the exact same object reference. This is what makes `distinctUntilChanged((a,b) => a?.id === b?.id)` in `EventModel` (`models/base.ts:116`) cheap and what lets `claimLatest` track an event by identity.
docs/research/applesauce/event-store-query-builders.md:37:The filter resolver (`getEventsForFilter`, lines 408-510) implements iterative AND with a key optimization at lines 470-486: when `authors × kinds <= 20`, use the composite `kindAuthor` index in a single pass instead of intersecting two large sets. This is the kind of micro-optimization NMP should plan for in `nmp-core`'s LMDB index choice.
docs/research/applesauce/event-store-query-builders.md:49:5. **NIP-01 tie-break, incoming-side** (lines 235-252): for replaceable kinds, compute the existing "winner" via `(created_at desc, id asc)`. If incoming does not beat the winner, swallow and (importantly) copy any cached symbols from the incoming event onto the winning instance.
docs/research/applesauce/event-store-query-builders.md:58:## 3. `EventMemory` claims — refcount-based GC anchor
docs/research/applesauce/event-store-query-builders.md:61:- `claims: WeakMap<NostrEvent, number>` (line 176, **a counter, not a boolean** — see gotchas §G2).
docs/research/applesauce/event-store-query-builders.md:62:- `claim()` increments + touches LRU (line 188).
docs/research/applesauce/event-store-query-builders.md:64:- `prune(limit)` iterates `unclaimed()` (which walks the LRU oldest-first) and removes (lines 217-242).
docs/research/applesauce/event-store-query-builders.md:68:The two RxJS operators that anchor claims:
docs/research/applesauce/event-store-query-builders.md:70:- `observable/claim-events.ts` — `claimEvents(claims)`: for streams of `NostrEvent | NostrEvent[]`, claim each unseen event in `tap`, release all on `finalize`. Used by `TimelineModel`.
docs/research/applesauce/event-store-query-builders.md:71:- `observable/claim-latest.ts` — `claimLatest(claims)`: for streams of `NostrEvent | undefined`, swap claim on every change (release old, claim new). Used by `EventModel` and `ReplaceableModel`.
docs/research/applesauce/event-store-query-builders.md:84:1. `hash_sum(args)` keys the cache (or `constructor.getKey(...args)` if provided — `OutboxModel` defines one at `models/outbox.ts:26-29` because its options object would otherwise key poorly).
docs/research/applesauce/event-store-query-builders.md:87:   - `finalize(cleanup)` — removes the entry from the cache when the inner observable terminates.
docs/research/applesauce/event-store-query-builders.md:90:That `share` config is the **subscription dedup magic**: all subscribers to the same `(constructor, key)` share one upstream and one ReplaySubject(1) cache. When the last subscriber unsubscribes, a 60-second warm-keep timer starts; if a new subscriber arrives within that window, no re-materialization happens. This is what makes calling `store.profile(pk)` from 50 React components result in one upstream pipeline.
docs/research/applesauce/event-store-query-builders.md:100:- `distinctUntilChanged` by id, `claimLatest` to pin.
docs/research/applesauce/event-store-query-builders.md:108:- Initial bulk fetch via `getTimeline`, claimed with `claimEvents`.
docs/research/applesauce/event-store-query-builders.md:116:## 6. The kind:3 + outbox composition — end-to-end
docs/research/applesauce/event-store-query-builders.md:118:When the application does `store.model(OutboxModel, user, { type: 'outbox', maxConnections: 5 })`:
docs/research/applesauce/event-store-query-builders.md:124:           └─> OutboxModel:    (models/outbox.ts:14-24)
docs/research/applesauce/event-store-query-builders.md:126:                includeMailboxes(store, 'outbox')  -> switchMap over the contact array, each
docs/research/applesauce/event-store-query-builders.md:136:- `includeMailboxes` uses `combineLatest(contacts.map(user => store.replaceable({kind:10002,pubkey:user.pubkey})...))`. That means **adding one contact spawns one new inner observable that itself goes through the shared-model cache**. If the same user is already mailbox-tracked by another model, the inner observable is the same shared instance — zero extra relay traffic.
docs/research/applesauce/event-store-query-builders.md:137:- The map-projection at `relay-selection.ts:32-43` returns the original `user` pointer when the kind:10002 hasn't loaded yet; it does **not** drop the contact. That's intentional — partial outbox knowledge still resolves *something*.
docs/research/applesauce/event-store-query-builders.md:139:- `OutboxModel.getKey` (`models/outbox.ts:26-29`) hashes only `[pubkey, type, maxConnections, maxRelaysPerUser]` — the blacklist and `score` function are intentionally excluded so they can be changed without forcing a new pipeline.
docs/research/applesauce/event-store-query-builders.md:141:This composition pattern is the actual deliverable for NMP. Reproducing the kind:3 special case alone misses the point — what NMP needs is the **mixin + share() + claim() + switchMap-into-models** substrate that allows users to write `MailboxesModel`, `OutboxModel`, and ten future models without each one wiring up its own insert/remove/dedup/share machinery.
docs/research/applesauce/event-store-query-builders.md:149:| `store.model(Constructor, ...args)` mixin extension point | the open question for `nmp-core`: how do downstream crates add a typed view kind without forking? |
docs/research/applesauce/event-store-query-builders.md:151:| `claim/touch/prune/unclaimed` LRU+refcount API | spec §7.5 claim-based GC |
docs/research/applesauce/event-store-query-builders.md:153:| `EventModels` mixin pattern | the LLM-friendliness test from `plan.md:148` — adding a new view kind without touching `nmp-core` |
docs/research/applesauce/event-store-query-builders.md:155:## 8. What this means for NMP's M2
docs/research/applesauce/event-store-query-builders.md:157:If `nmp-core` ships only the EventStore + planner without the model-cache + claim layer, every consumer will independently materialize its own per-view pipeline, and the framework will not deliver the "reactive-by-default, GC-safe-by-default" experience the spec promises. The model-cache layer is small (`event-models.ts` is 150 LOC, `claim-events.ts`+`claim-latest.ts` are <80 combined) but architectural — it must be part of Phase 1, not deferred.
docs/research/ndk/gotchas.md:19:`getRelayListForUsers` timeout fired before EOSE arrived from relays → empty relay lists → subscriptions never connecting to user relays. docs/research/applesauce/gotchas.md:12:## G2. Event claims: counter vs boolean = leak vs over-eviction
docs/research/applesauce/gotchas.md:14:**Commit `75ef7d5f`** ("Convert event claims to counter to avoid memory leaks"). Pre-fix: claims were a boolean (`Set<NostrEvent>` semantics). If two subscriptions claimed the same event and one unsubscribed, the boolean cleared and the LRU pruner could evict the event while the second subscription was still bound to it. Fix: refcount via `WeakMap<NostrEvent, number>`. Decrement to zero deletes the entry; non-zero keeps the event pinned.
docs/research/applesauce/gotchas.md:16:**Lesson:** NMP's claim-based GC (spec §7.5) must use refcounts, not a presence flag. The `WeakMap` choice is also important — it lets events get GC'd via JS GC if every reference is dropped, which is the safety net for the case where claims are correctly balanced but the consumer holds no other reference.
docs/research/applesauce/gotchas.md:20:**Commit `d2322cee`** ("fix: pool manual methods silently dropping offline relays") + commit `c2bd9a2a` ("Ignore unreachable (ready=false) relays by default"). The pool's `subscription`/`request`/`publish`/`count`/`sync` were calling `group()` without passing `ignoreOffline=false`. `RelayPool.ignoreOffline` defaults to true, so any relay with `ready=false` was silently filtered out. The caller then hung forever waiting for events that could never arrive because no relay was actually subscribed. Later commit `65534509` ("fix(relay): wait for non-ready relays in RelayPool.group") changed semantics again so that not-yet-ready relays are *included* as soon as they become ready, rather than dropped.
docs/research/applesauce/gotchas.md:38:**Commit `a41f3b70`** ("fix bug with restoring encrypted content did not unlock events"). The encrypted-content cache existed but its restoration on rehydration didn't fire `update$`, so consumers subscribed via `watchEventUpdates` (`observable/watch-event-updates.ts`) never saw the now-unlocked hidden contacts. The `HiddenContactsModel` (`models/contacts.ts:28-36`) explicitly relies on `watchEventUpdates`.
docs/research/applesauce/gotchas.md:40:Related: commit `a959bb22` ("Fix many NIP-60 bugs Fix bug with hidden tags cache symbol") and `c9c0aba5` ("strip stale symbol caches in EventFactory.chain()") — the symbol-cache pattern (`hidden-tags.ts`, `cache.ts`) is powerful but creates a category of bugs where a stale cache survives a mutation it should invalidate.
docs/research/applesauce/gotchas.md:42:**Lesson:** Any cache-on-symbol pattern in NMP needs an explicit invalidation hook called from every mutation site. The notify-update pattern (`helpers/event.ts:145-150` — `notifyEventUpdate` finds the parent store and calls `update`) is the right shape.
docs/research/applesauce/gotchas.md:46:**Reading `signers/password-signer.ts:39-74`** (no specific bugfix commit, design observation). `requestUnlock()` creates a deferred and stores it, but `unlock()` doesn't resolve it. Instead, the next call to a method that called `requestUnlock()` re-checks `if (this.key) return`, which now returns immediately. This works because all signing methods `await this.requestUnlock()` *then* re-read `this.key`, but it's a subtle invariant — if a future refactor caches `unlockPromise` and awaits it without re-checking `this.key`, the queued operations will hang forever.
docs/research/applesauce/gotchas.md:56:## G9. ActionRunner cached context across account swaps
docs/research/applesauce/gotchas.md:58:**Commit `96120548`** ("Fix ActionRunner cache causing actions to have wrong `user` when accounts change"). `ActionRunner.getContext()` memoized the context (`action-runner.ts:54-68` — `if (this._context) return this._context;`). When the user swapped accounts, actions ran with the previous account's `user`/`self`. Fix (in the broader commit family for cast cleanup): the global `User.cache` (`casts/user.ts:17`) needed beforeEach clearing in tests; in production, the ActionRunner is short-lived per account.
docs/research/applesauce/gotchas.md:60:**Lesson:** Per-account context caching is fine; cross-account caching is a bug. NMP's `ActionRunner` analogue must rebuild context (or invalidate it) on every active-account change. Make this a contract: subscribe to `AccountManager.active$`, drop the cache on every emission.
docs/research/applesauce/gotchas.md:62:## G10. EventFactory symbol-cache leak across pipeline steps
docs/research/applesauce/gotchas.md:64:**Commit `c9c0aba5`** ("strip stale symbol caches in EventFactory.chain() and replace removed buildEvent usages"). `EventFactory.chain()` carried symbol caches between operations. If step 1 set `HiddenTagsSymbol` and step 2 added new tags, step 2 would mutate the underlying tags but step 3 would see the stale cache. Fix: strip `PRESERVE_EVENT_SYMBOLS` after each step.
docs/research/applesauce/gotchas.md:66:**Lesson:** NMP's event-builder pipeline should either operate on immutable inputs or have a per-step invalidation. The "cache on symbols" approach is fast but requires discipline.
docs/research/applesauce/gotchas.md:84:**Lesson:** Symbol attachment, claim, and emission must happen in this order: attach → emit → consumer can act. Any reorder breaks consumers.
docs/research/applesauce/gotchas.md:110:## G18. ExtensionSigner pubkey not cached
docs/research/applesauce/gotchas.md:112:**Commit `0867a502`** ("Cache the pubkey on ExtensionSigner"). Every getPublicKey() round-tripped to the extension. For an action that called `getPublicKey()` three times, three prompts. Fix: cache after first success.
docs/research/applesauce/gotchas.md:151:3. **Caches without invalidation hooks** (G6, G10, G9, G11) — every cache needs an invalidation contract.
docs/research/applesauce/gotchas.md:155:NMP's M2 design review should explicitly check each new component against these five categories.
docs/research/ndk/kind3-auto-tracking.md:3:This file documents the two NMP-load-bearing claims: (1) native listening to kind:3 changes for the active user, and (2) auto-update of open subscriptions when the follow list changes.

docs/research/ndk/kind3-auto-tracking.md:96:This is the user's second claim. The honest version:
docs/research/ndk/kind3-auto-tracking.md:164:**For NMP, the framework-magic contract should hide this glue entirely behind a primitive like `FollowsFeed` or a generated wrapper like `useFollowsFeed()` — so the app DOES dispatch zero code while the kernel does the stop/restart on kind:3 arrival.** This is the load-bearing NMP-side addition; see `docs/design/framework-magic.md` for the contract.
docs/research/ndk/kind3-auto-tracking.md:172:this.outboxTracker.on("user:relay-list-updated", (pubkey, _outboxItem) => {
docs/research/applesauce/outbox.md:7:Applesauce's outbox is not a relay-resolver service. It is a **reactive composition of three RxJS operators** over the EventStore. There is no central "outbox service" — there is just `OutboxModel = contacts() ⇒ includeMailboxes() ⇒ selectOptimalRelays()`. Every consumer that wants outbox routing subscribes to the model directly.
docs/research/applesauce/outbox.md:15:  .pipe(map(event => event && { inboxes: getInboxes(event), outboxes: getOutboxes(event) }));
docs/research/applesauce/outbox.md:18:Reads a kind:10002 via the generic `replaceable()` query-builder and projects into `{inboxes, outboxes}`. Re-emits on any kind:10002 update.
docs/research/applesauce/outbox.md:29:### `OutboxModel(user, opts)` — `packages/core/src/models/outbox.ts:14-24`
docs/research/applesauce/outbox.md:39:That's the entire outbox model.
docs/research/applesauce/outbox.md:52:          const relays = type === "outbox" ? getOutboxes(event) : getInboxes(event);
docs/research/applesauce/outbox.md:64:1. **Per-contact independent subscription.** Each contact becomes its own `replaceable()` subscription via the shared model cache. Following a new user triggers exactly one new kind:10002 subscription (none if another model already had that user mailbox-tracked).
docs/research/applesauce/outbox.md:65:2. **Graceful degradation on missing mailbox.** If no kind:10002 has loaded yet, the original `ProfilePointer` is returned with whatever relays it had. The outbox model never blocks on missing mailboxes; it routes with partial knowledge and re-emits when the kind:10002 arrives.
docs/research/applesauce/outbox.md:66:3. **Re-emission on every change.** `combineLatest` re-emits on any inner change. NMP must size its planner debouncer accordingly — naive re-resolution on each kind:10002 will thrash; `OutboxModel` itself doesn't debounce, downstream consumers do via the model-cache 60s keep-warm.
docs/research/applesauce/outbox.md:100:- `createFilterMap(outboxMap, filter)` (lines 138-145) — pivots to `{ relay: { authors: [pubkeys], ...filter } }` for batched per-relay REQs.
docs/research/applesauce/outbox.md:104:## 6. Timeline loaders consume the outbox
docs/research/applesauce/outbox.md:108:- `loadBlocksFromOutboxMap(pool, outboxes$, filter, opts)` (lines 290-312) — accepts an `Observable<OutboxMap>` and re-projects to a `FilterMap` on every change. Internally caches per-relay loaders so unchanged relay+filter pairs reuse their existing forward/backward block state (line 269-281).
docs/research/applesauce/outbox.md:109:- `loadBlocksFromOutboxMapCache` (lines 315-352) — same but for the local cache, with a single merged-pubkey query rather than per-relay splitting.
docs/research/applesauce/outbox.md:110:- `createOutboxTimelineLoader` (lines 455-477) — public wrapper that combines cache and relay loaders.
docs/research/applesauce/outbox.md:112:The `cache` at lines 269-281 is the **incremental-resubscription cache**: when the OutboxMap changes (e.g., one contact's mailbox updated), only the affected relays get new loaders; the rest reuse cached forward/backward cursor state. NMP's planner must do the same to avoid full re-pagination on every kind:10002.
docs/research/applesauce/outbox.md:116:Applesauce's `ActionContext.publish` (`packages/actions/src/action-runner.ts:71-95`) accepts an optional `relays` arg. The actions themselves resolve outbox before calling publish:
docs/research/applesauce/outbox.md:121:  const [event, outboxes] = await Promise.all([
docs/research/applesauce/outbox.md:123:    user.outboxes$.$first(1000, undefined),
docs/research/applesauce/outbox.md:125:  return [event ? ContactsFactory.modify(event) : ContactsFactory.create(), outboxes];
docs/research/applesauce/outbox.md:131:    const [factory, outboxes] = await modifyContacts(context);
docs/research/applesauce/outbox.md:133:    await context.publish(signed, outboxes);
docs/research/applesauce/outbox.md:138:Note that this is **the caller's responsibility**, not the framework's — Applesauce does not have a global "publish-uses-outbox-by-default" hook. NMP's spec `aim.md:123` ("by default and automatically") is a stronger guarantee than Applesauce delivers; the spec's design is correct, but NMP cannot just copy Applesauce's `publish(event, relays?)` — it must default to outbox resolution and require an opt-out, not opt-in.
docs/research/applesauce/outbox.md:140:## 8. Inbox routing for DMs
docs/research/applesauce/outbox.md:142:Symmetrically, `MailboxesModel` returns `inboxes` and `includeMailboxes(store, 'inbox')` does the same composition for the inbox side. NMP's deferred DM milestone needs to wire publishes to a recipient via `addressable -> recipient kind:10002 -> inboxes`. Applesauce expects the caller to do this manually per-action; NMP should bake it into the publish path itself when DMs un-defer.
docs/research/applesauce/outbox.md:146:- **No relay scoring beyond user-supplied score().** No RTT tracking, no NIP-66 monitor support, no per-relay error rate. The `applesauce-relay/liveness.ts` package (175 LOC) tracks healthy/unhealthy/dead but doesn't feed back into outbox selection automatically.
docs/research/applesauce/outbox.md:147:- **No write-set bias.** `OutboxModel` projects every contact onto a single max-N relay set, regardless of which contacts the consumer is actually reading. There's no "filter the outbox to only contacts I'm displaying right now" — that's the consumer's job.
docs/research/applesauce/outbox.md:148:- **No outbox cache TTL or staleness check.** Once `MailboxesModel` has emitted, only `update$`/`insert$` for that specific kind:10002 changes it. There's no periodic refresh.
docs/research/applesauce/outbox.md:149:- **No fallback to legacy NIP-02 relay JSON.** `getRelaysFromContactsEvent` exists at `helpers/contacts.ts:19-38` and is parsed by `OutboxModel` callers manually if they want to fall back, but `MailboxesModel` strictly reads kind:10002. The user must opt in via the `includeLegacyWriteRelays` modifier (living in `applesauce-loaders/src/operators/outbox-modifiers.ts`).
docs/research/applesauce/outbox.md:153:1. The outbox engine in `nmp-core` must be reactive at every layer, not just at "give me a relay list" boundary. Applesauce's `OutboxModel` re-emits on contacts-change AND on per-contact-mailbox-change. A snapshot API will not suffice for the spec's "subscriptions automatically re-resolve" guarantee (`aim.md:125`).
docs/research/applesauce/outbox.md:156:4. The "publish to outbox + recipient inboxes by default" guarantee is **stronger than Applesauce's**. Don't copy Applesauce's caller-responsibility model — bake it into the planner.

docs/design/framework-magic.md:81:- `outbox.md` §2 — `TBD-from-research(ndk/kind3-auto-tracking.md)`: how NDK rebinds in-flight REQs when an author's mailbox arrives mid-subscription.

docs/design/framework-magic.md:91:- This document does **not** introduce new types or traits — `PublishPlanner`, `ViewModule`, `LogicalInterest`, `SubscriptionCompiler`, `MailboxCache`, `KeyringCapability` are already defined in the cited design docs and product spec. The contract uses those names.
docs/design/framework-magic/sessions.md:13:- `Trigger::ActiveAccountChanged { from, to }` (`subscription-compilation/recompilation.md` §4.2) fires as a consequence of the state change. The planner re-runs `interests()` on every `ViewModule` whose registered interest carries `InterestScope::ActiveAccount` (`subscription-compilation/intro.md` §2.1 line 60 + §2.3); `InterestScope::Account(specific)` and `InterestScope::Global` interests are untouched.
docs/design/framework-magic/sessions.md:41:C12 is the most direct demonstration of cardinal doctrine **D4** ("single writer per fact; caches derive"). The "fact" is `SessionState.active`. The "caches" are every active-account-scoped view, every signer binding, every relay-routing decision. The framework's job is to make sure every cache derives mechanically; the app's job is to write the fact once.
docs/design/framework-magic/sessions.md:62:- **Background account state** (per-account sync watermarks, per-account action ledger). Those are per-account scopes inside the storage backend; the contract does not specify the scoping mechanism, only that the switch does not leak state across.

docs/design/lmdb/watermarks.md:1:# LMDB sub-design: watermarks, provenance, migrations
docs/design/lmdb/watermarks.md:3:> Part of [`docs/design/lmdb-schema.md`](../lmdb-schema.md). Covers the three NMP-owned LMDB sub-databases that hold non-event durable state: `watermarks`, `provenance`, and the per-`DomainModule` sub-databases tracked by `_meta`.
docs/design/lmdb/watermarks.md:7:Sub-db: `watermarks`. Populated by the M4 NIP-77 negentropy engine and consulted by the M2 subscription planner (per `docs/product-spec/subsystems.md` §7.2 "coverage-aware backfill").
docs/design/lmdb/watermarks.md:19:    pub last_negentropy_state: Option<Vec<u8>>, // engine-opaque resume blob (M4)
docs/design/lmdb/watermarks.md:25:`last_negentropy_state` is an opaque byte blob written by the NIP-77 engine (M4) — the store does not interpret it. Empty for `ReqScan` / `Manual` rows.
docs/design/lmdb/watermarks.md:33:    match self.read_watermark(key) {
docs/design/lmdb/watermarks.md:47:On `LmdbEventStore::open()`, the store reads all `watermarks` rows and builds an in-memory `HashMap<WatermarkKey, WatermarkRow>` for hot lookups. Every `write_watermark` updates both the in-memory map and the LMDB row in a single `RwTxn`. Restart re-derives the map; we don't need a separate cache file.
docs/design/lmdb/watermarks.md:49:For installations with O(100k+) watermarks (an edge case — typical apps see O(100)–O(10k)), the in-memory map switches to a lazy-loaded variant that pages on demand. Threshold and switching logic deferred to M4 when the negentropy engine's real-world row count is measured.
docs/design/lmdb/watermarks.md:80:### 2.2 Reuse in outbox routing (M2)
docs/design/lmdb/watermarks.md:95:This produces a deterministic hash that is stable across `Filter` field-order variations and across Rust HashMap ordering randomness. The implementation lives at `crates/nmp-core/src/store/watermarks.rs::canonical_filter_hash(&Filter) -> [u8; 32]` and is the single source of truth for the planner + sync engine + dump format.
docs/design/lmdb/watermarks.md:97:A filter with `limit: Some(N)` produces a *different* hash than the same filter without `limit` — because their cache-coverage semantics genuinely differ. A planner that wants to share a watermark across "limit=200" and "limit=500" requests of the same shape strips `limit` before hashing (this is a planner-side optimisation, not a store-side one).
docs/design/lmdb/watermarks.md:179:The kernel's internal LMDB layout (provenance + secondaries + tombstones + watermarks) is itself versioned via the reserved `_kernel` namespace in `_meta`. Current version: `1`. A future schema change (e.g., a new secondary index) bumps this and runs a one-time rebuild from primary events.
docs/design/lmdb/watermarks.md:189:- `StoreHealth.watermark_count` (per [`gc.md`](gc.md) §7) summarises the global count.
docs/design/lmdb/watermarks.md:191:These are read-mostly paths; the only contention is between the actor's `write_watermark` calls (driven by M4 sync completions) and the diagnostics query, which is bounded by LMDB's MVCC reader semantics — no lock contention.

docs/design/lmdb/tests.md:125:### 2.9 Watermarks (§7.1 "Sync watermarks")

docs/design/lmdb/tests.md:131:- Test `coverage()`: row with `synced_up_to = now - 60s` → `Coverage::CompleteAsOf` (under default 300s staleness); row with `synced_up_to = now - 600s` → `Coverage::PartialUpTo`; missing row → `Coverage::Unknown`.
docs/design/lmdb/tests.md:132:- `list_watermarks_for_relay("wss://a/")` returns only rows for that relay.
docs/design/lmdb/tests.md:137:File: `crates/nmp-testing/tests/store_gc_claims.rs`
docs/design/lmdb/tests.md:142:- Assert: 10 claimed events still present in hot (`store.get_by_id` is a fast in-memory hit — measurable via a counter exposed for the test); 40 unclaimed events evicted from LRU but still readable from disk.
docs/design/lmdb/tests.md:144:- Assert: previously claimed events now subject to LRU eviction.
docs/design/lmdb/tests.md:150:- Build a populated store: 1000 events, 50 tombstones, 100 watermarks, 200 domain rows across 3 namespaces.
docs/design/lmdb/tests.md:187:- Run for 60 seconds with light churn (insert 10 events / sec).
docs/design/reactivity/scheduling-and-data-model.md:25:- **Time-based:** `now - last_flush >= flush_interval` (default 16ms = ~60Hz).
docs/design/reactivity/scheduling-and-data-model.md:53:Per-view delta budget: ≤ 60 deltas/sec/view (matches the 60Hz flush). Total `ViewBatch` size scales with active view count; no absolute ceiling.
docs/design/reactivity/scheduling-and-data-model.md:60:- On next tick, emit a single `FullState` snapshot.
docs/design/reactivity/scheduling-and-data-model.md:63:This is lossless: the `FullState` snapshot includes every open view's current payload, so the platform's shadow ends up in the same state it would have via deltas.
docs/design/reactivity/scheduling-and-data-model.md:87:│   - View payloads in actor's view registry               │
docs/design/reactivity/scheduling-and-data-model.md:95:│     tombstones, sync watermarks                          │
docs/design/reactivity/scheduling-and-data-model.md:105:- **Subscription lifecycle is refcounted per tier.** Component refcount in Tier 3 drives `OpenView`/`CloseView` to Rust; Rust's claim count in Tier 2 drives planner REQ subscriptions to relays; relay REQs on the wire are the bottom of the stack.
docs/design/reactivity/scheduling-and-data-model.md:113:- **Hot:** events referenced by any open view's claim set, plus a configurable recency window (default: most recent 5,000 events globally).
docs/design/reactivity/scheduling-and-data-model.md:115:- **Eviction:** LRU among hot events not currently claimed. Claimed events are never evicted.

docs/design/lmdb/gc.md:139:Restart recovery: `claims_meta` sub-db ([`keys.md`](keys.md) §1) holds the persisted per-`ClaimerId` pin set. On startup the actor rebuilds active views first (per the diagnostics replay sequence), then re-claims; entries in `claims_meta` whose `ClaimerId` is not associated with a re-opened view are dropped from the persisted map. This means the cold-start path always re-derives claims from open-view state, but the persistence is what lets the store survive an actor restart without losing hot-set protection mid-shutdown.

     8	These are not "missing" — they're the deliverables. Listed here because they constrain the architecture.
     9	
    10	1. **Model-cache mixin pattern.** `event-models.ts:40-150`. NMP must expose an extension point so downstream crates (or LLM-generated views per `plan.md`) can register new typed views (`MutesView`, `ZapsView`, `WalletView`) without forking `nmp-core`. Applesauce does this via TypeScript prototype augmentation; NMP's equivalent in Rust is a `View` trait + registry.
    11	2. **`share()` with keepWarm + ReplaySubject(1) semantics.** `event-models.ts:73-78`. Every typed view subscription must dedupe across consumers, replay last value to new subscribers, and stay warm for ~60s after the last unsubscribe.
    12	3. **Claim refcount + LRU prune.** `event-memory.ts:176-242`, `observable/claim-*.ts`. Separate from RxJS refcounting. NMP's planner must claim every event surfaced through a view and release on view drop.
    13	4. **Single-instance invariant via `mapToMemory`.** `event-store.ts:136-142`. Every read of the same event id returns the same `&Event` so identity-equality is meaningful. In Rust this is `Arc<Event>` interning.
    14	5. **NIP-01 tie-break in both insertion directions.** `event-store.ts:235-301`. Pre-check and post-cleanup. Both async and sync paths.
    80	modelKeepWarm = 60_000;
    81	```
    82	
    83	`model(constructor, ...args)` (lines 50-86):
    84	1. `hash_sum(args)` keys the cache (or `constructor.getKey(...args)` if provided — `OutboxModel` defines one at `models/outbox.ts:26-29` because its options object would otherwise key poorly).
    85	2. If a model already exists for `(constructor, key)`, return it.
    86	3. Otherwise call `constructor(...args)(this)` to materialize the observable, then wrap with:
    87	   - `finalize(cleanup)` — removes the entry from the cache when the inner observable terminates.
    88	   - `share({ connector: () => new ReplaySubject(1), resetOnComplete: () => timer(60_000), resetOnRefCountZero: () => timer(60_000) })`.
    60	```
    61	
    62	Three properties matter:
    63	
    64	1. **Per-contact independent subscription.** Each contact becomes its own `replaceable()` subscription via the shared model cache. Following a new user triggers exactly one new kind:10002 subscription (none if another model already had that user mailbox-tracked).
    65	2. **Graceful degradation on missing mailbox.** If no kind:10002 has loaded yet, the original `ProfilePointer` is returned with whatever relays it had. The outbox model never blocks on missing mailboxes; it routes with partial knowledge and re-emits when the kind:10002 arrives.
    66	3. **Re-emission on every change.** `combineLatest` re-emits on any inner change. NMP must size its planner debouncer accordingly — naive re-resolution on each kind:10002 will thrash; `OutboxModel` itself doesn't debounce, downstream consumers do via the model-cache 60s keep-warm.
    67	
    68	## 3. `selectOptimalRelays` — greedy set-cover heuristic

     1	import hash_sum from "hash-sum";
     2	import { identity, map } from "rxjs";
     3	import { Model } from "../event-store/interface.js";
     4	import { ProfilePointer } from "../helpers/pointers.js";
     5	import { selectOptimalRelays, SelectOptimalRelaysOptions } from "../helpers/relay-selection.js";
     6	import { ignoreBlacklistedRelays, includeMailboxes } from "../observable/relay-selection.js";
     7	
     8	export type OutboxModelOptions = SelectOptimalRelaysOptions & {
     9	  type?: "inbox" | "outbox";
    10	  blacklist?: Parameters<typeof ignoreBlacklistedRelays>[0];
    11	};
    12	
    13	/** A model that returns the users contacts with the relays to connect to */
    14	export function OutboxModel(user: string | ProfilePointer, opts: OutboxModelOptions): Model<ProfilePointer[]> {
    15	  return (store) =>
    16	    store.contacts(user).pipe(
    17	      /** Ignore blacklisted relays */
    18	      opts?.blacklist ? ignoreBlacklistedRelays(opts.blacklist) : identity,
    19	      /** Include mailboxes */
    20	      includeMailboxes(store, opts.type),
    21	      /** Select the optimal relays */
    22	      map((users) => selectOptimalRelays(users, opts)),
    23	    );
    24	}
    25	
    26	OutboxModel.getKey = (user: string | ProfilePointer, opts: OutboxModelOptions) => {
    27	  const p = typeof user === "string" ? user : user.pubkey;
    28	  return hash_sum([p, opts.type, opts.maxConnections, opts.maxRelaysPerUser]);
    29	};

 succeeded in 0ms:
     1	import {
     2	  combineLatest,
     3	  combineLatestWith,
     4	  isObservable,
     5	  map,
     6	  of,
     7	  pipe,
     8	  switchMap,
     9	  type MonoTypeOperatorFunction,
    10	  type Observable,
    11	  type OperatorFunction,
    12	} from "rxjs";
    13	import { IEventSubscriptions } from "../event-store/interface.js";
    14	import { getInboxes, getOutboxes } from "../helpers/mailboxes.js";
    15	import { addRelayHintsToPointer, ProfilePointer } from "../helpers/pointers.js";
    16	import { removeBlacklistedRelays, selectOptimalRelays, setFallbackRelays } from "../helpers/relay-selection.js";
    17	
    18	/** RxJS operator that fetches outboxes for profile pointers from the event store */
    19	export function includeMailboxes(
    20	  store: IEventSubscriptions,
    21	  type: "inbox" | "outbox" = "outbox",
    22	): OperatorFunction<ProfilePointer[], ProfilePointer[]> {
    23	  // Get the outboxes for all contacts
    24	  return switchMap((contacts) =>
    25	    combineLatest(
    26	      contacts.map((user) =>
    27	        // Subscribe to the outboxes for the user
    28	        store
    29	          .replaceable({
    30	            kind: 10002,
    31	            pubkey: user.pubkey,
    32	          })
    33	          .pipe(
    34	            // Add the relays to the user
    35	            map((event) => {
    36	              if (!event) return user;
    37	
    38	              // Get the relays from the event
    39	              const relays = type === "outbox" ? getOutboxes(event) : getInboxes(event);
    40	              if (!relays) return user;
    41	
    42	              // Add the relays to the user
    43	              return addRelayHintsToPointer(user, relays);
    44	            }),
    45	          ),
    46	      ),
    47	    ),
    48	  );
    49	}
    50	
    51	/** Removes blacklisted relays from the user's relays */
    52	export function ignoreBlacklistedRelays(
    53	  blacklist: string[] | Observable<string[]>,
    54	): MonoTypeOperatorFunction<ProfilePointer[]> {
    55	  return pipe(
    56	    // Combine with the observable so it re-emits when the blacklist changes
    57	    combineLatestWith(isObservable(blacklist) ? blacklist : of(blacklist)),
    58	    // Filter the relays for the user
    59	    map(([users, blacklist]) => removeBlacklistedRelays(users, blacklist)),
    60	  );
    61	}
    62	
    63	/** Sets fallback relays for any user that has 0 relays */
    64	export function includeFallbackRelays(
    65	  fallbacks: string[] | Observable<string[]>,
    66	): MonoTypeOperatorFunction<ProfilePointer[]> {
    67	  return pipe(
    68	    // Get the fallbacks from the observable
    69	    combineLatestWith(isObservable(fallbacks) ? fallbacks : of(fallbacks)),
    70	    // Set the fallback relays for the users
    71	    map(([users, fallbacks]) => setFallbackRelays(users, fallbacks)),
    72	  );
    73	}
    74	
    75	/** A operator calls {@link selectOptimalRelays} and filters the relays for the user */
    76	export function filterOptimalRelays(
    77	  maxConnections: number | Observable<number>,
    78	  maxRelaysPerUser: number | Observable<number>,
    79	): MonoTypeOperatorFunction<ProfilePointer[]> {
    80	  return pipe(
    81	    // Combine with the observable so it re-emits when the max connections and max relays per user change
    82	    combineLatestWith(
    83	      isObservable(maxConnections) ? maxConnections : of(maxConnections),
    84	      isObservable(maxRelaysPerUser) ? maxRelaysPerUser : of(maxRelaysPerUser),
    85	    ),
    86	    // Filter the relays for the user
    87	    map(([users, maxConnections, maxRelaysPerUser]) =>
    88	      selectOptimalRelays(users, { maxConnections, maxRelaysPerUser }),
    89	    ),
    90	  );

   134	Key observations for NMP:
   135	
   136	- `includeMailboxes` uses `combineLatest(contacts.map(user => store.replaceable({kind:10002,pubkey:user.pubkey})...))`. That means **adding one contact spawns one new inner observable that itself goes through the shared-model cache**. If the same user is already mailbox-tracked by another model, the inner observable is the same shared instance — zero extra relay traffic.
   137	- The map-projection at `relay-selection.ts:32-43` returns the original `user` pointer when the kind:10002 hasn't loaded yet; it does **not** drop the contact. That's intentional — partial outbox knowledge still resolves *something*.
   138	- `selectOptimalRelays` (`helpers/relay-selection.ts:14-93`) is a greedy set-cover: each iteration picks the relay covering the most uncovered users, optionally biased by `score(relay, coverage, popularity)`. `maxRelaysPerUser` caps per-user concentration. The TODO at line 89 acknowledges that the final per-user relay list may exceed `maxRelaysPerUser` because the count is enforced during selection, not after.
   139	- `OutboxModel.getKey` (`models/outbox.ts:26-29`) hashes only `[pubkey, type, maxConnections, maxRelaysPerUser]` — the blacklist and `score` function are intentionally excluded so they can be changed without forcing a new pipeline.
   140	
   141	This composition pattern is the actual deliverable for NMP. Reproducing the kind:3 special case alone misses the point — what NMP needs is the **mixin + share() + claim() + switchMap-into-models** substrate that allows users to write `MailboxesModel`, `OutboxModel`, and ten future models without each one wiring up its own insert/remove/dedup/share machinery.

    40	
    41	### D1. Best-effort rendering — render now, refine in place
    42	
    43	Apps built with this framework **never withhold cached data and never block on fetches**. Every view payload field carries a value, not a "loading" status. Missing display names default to a shortened npub; missing pictures default to a deterministic identicon URI; missing timestamps default to "now". When a more authoritative value (e.g., the author's kind:0) arrives later, the view payload updates in place and the affected cell re-renders. The UI never sees a spinner gating already-renderable content.
    44	
    45	The doctrine is enforced by the view payload **types**: display fields are non-`Option`, placeholders are part of the type contract, and freshness is exposed (when relevant) as an optional badge hint, not a render gate. There is no `if has_profile { render } else { spinner }` pattern available in the API — the framework does not provide one.
    46	
    10	**Statement.** Every display-bearing field of every view payload is **non-`Option`** and carries either an authoritative value or a defined placeholder. When the authoritative value later arrives — a kind:0 for an author, kind:9735 zap receipts for a note, the decrypted body for a DM — the same payload re-emits with the field updated in place. The platform's reactive primitive (`@Observable` / `Flow` / signals) sees the change and only the affected cell re-renders. **No spinner ever gates an already-rendered cell, and no view module ever exposes a `loading: bool` to the platform.**
    11	
    12	**Framework does:**
    13	
    14	- The placeholder contract at `docs/product-spec/subsystems.md` §7.6 lines 181–192 (the seven-row table: display name → npub-shortened, picture → identicon URI, NIP-05 → empty string, timestamp → "just now", reaction count → 0, zap total → 0 sats, content body → empty string).
    15	- The view-payload typing at `subsystems.md` §7.6 lines 199–222 (the `TimelineItem` example with all fields non-`Option` except the optional `repost_of` / `quote_of` semantic-Option markers).
    16	- The freshness surface at `subsystems.md` §7.6 line 196 (`xxx_freshness: FreshnessHint` is an optional **sibling** field; UI may render a badge; the framework never withholds the value).
    17	- The in-place refinement mechanism: `ViewModule::on_projection_changed` (`docs/design/kernel-substrate.md` §3 lines 148–150). When a kind:0 lands for author X, the kernel's projection cache (a shared cross-view projection) updates X's display name; every view module that lists items by X re-runs `on_projection_changed`, produces a delta, and the wire-emitter sends a `ViewBatch` with the updated field.
    18	- The platform-shadow domain key (`kernel-substrate.md` §3 line 128 `fn key(spec: &Self::Spec) -> Self::Key`) ensures the cell-level re-render is targeted: the platform's reactive primitive updates only the row whose key matches, not the entire list.

    88	`encryptionEnabled(scheme?)` returns the list of schemes the signer supports. Pattern: check before calling encrypt, fall back to NIP-04 if NIP-44 unavailable. Most callers use `EncryptionMethod`-typed helpers in `core/src/events/encryption.ts`.
    89	
    90	## Implications for NMP
    91	
    92	- **Signer interface is generous**: NMP can implement Swift/Kotlin signers that conform to a translated `NDKSigner` protocol. The hard part is faithful NIP-46 if NMP wants remote-signing parity.
    93	- **NIP-46 round-trip** is async and times out — UX needs spinners, not blocking modals.
    94	- **NIP-07 doesn't exist on mobile** — equivalents are NIP-55 (Android intent), Lightning Wallet-style intent flows on iOS, or a custom in-app signer.
    95	- **Serialization** is the cleanest cross-platform contract: store `{ type, payload }` JSON, reconstruct on app restart. Mobile equivalent must produce the same payload schema if cross-app interop is wanted.
    96	- **bunker:// URL parse and connection flow** is a one-action UX in NDK (`NDKNip46Signer.bunker(ndk, uri)`) — NMP framework-magic must give apps the same one-call onboarding.

docs/research/applesauce/gotchas.md:8:**Commit `90d525af`** ("fix(core): implement NIP-01 tie-break for replaceable events"). Pre-fix, when an incoming replaceable event had the same `created_at` as the stored one, the store rejected the incoming unconditionally. Two clients independently producing a replaceable within the same second each kept only their own; the other was silently dropped on arrival from a relay. The fix (`event-store/event-store.ts:235-301` and the mirrored block in `async-event-store.ts:198-264`) does two passes: pre-insert "does anything beat me?" and post-insert "find the winner across all stored versions and remove losers."
docs/research/applesauce/gotchas.md:20:**Commit `d2322cee`** ("fix: pool manual methods silently dropping offline relays") + commit `c2bd9a2a` ("Ignore unreachable (ready=false) relays by default"). The pool's `subscription`/`request`/`publish`/`count`/`sync` were calling `group()` without passing `ignoreOffline=false`. `RelayPool.ignoreOffline` defaults to true, so any relay with `ready=false` was silently filtered out. The caller then hung forever waiting for events that could never arrive because no relay was actually subscribed. Later commit `65534509` ("fix(relay): wait for non-ready relays in RelayPool.group") changed semantics again so that not-yet-ready relays are *included* as soon as they become ready, rather than dropped.
docs/research/applesauce/gotchas.md:26:**Commit `b03c0d96`** ("Fix timeline backwards loader not handling `until` correctly on filters"). Pre-fix: after loading a block, the next `until` was set to the oldest event's `created_at`, but NIP-01 defines `until` as **inclusive**, so the same event would be returned again at the boundary, causing an infinite loop on singleton blocks. Fix at `loaders/timeline-loader.ts:107`: `if (minCreatedAt !== undefined) cursor = minCreatedAt - 1;`.
docs/research/applesauce/gotchas.md:36:## G6. Hidden tags: encrypted content unlock didn't propagate
docs/research/applesauce/gotchas.md:46:**Reading `signers/password-signer.ts:39-74`** (no specific bugfix commit, design observation). `requestUnlock()` creates a deferred and stores it, but `unlock()` doesn't resolve it. Instead, the next call to a method that called `requestUnlock()` re-checks `if (this.key) return`, which now returns immediately. This works because all signing methods `await this.requestUnlock()` *then* re-read `this.key`, but it's a subtle invariant — if a future refactor caches `unlockPromise` and awaits it without re-checking `this.key`, the queued operations will hang forever.
docs/research/applesauce/gotchas.md:94:**Commit `1ff4283f`** + the changeset in `c2bd9a2a`. Default retry count was 10, leading to long blocking on dead relays. Lowered to 3.
docs/research/applesauce/gotchas.md:96:**Lesson:** Defaults matter. NMP's default retry should be small (≤3) with explicit override for "really want to wait."

 succeeded in 0ms:
    70	}
    71	
    72	/** If event is undefined, attempt to load using the fallback loader */
    73	function loadEventUsingFallback(
    74	  store: IMissingEventLoader,
    75	  pointer: EventPointer | AddressPointer | AddressPointerWithoutD,
    76	): MonoTypeOperatorFunction<NostrEvent | undefined> {
    77	  return switchMap((event) => {
    78	    if (event) return of(event);
    79	
    80	    // If no loader pass value through, should never happen
    81	    if (!store.eventLoader) return of(event);
    82	
    83	    // If event was not found, attempt to load
    84	    return from(store.eventLoader(pointer)).pipe(
    85	      // Start with `undefined` since its not loaded yet
    86	      startWith(undefined),
    87	    );
    88	  });
    89	}
    90	
    91	/** A model that returns a single event or undefined when its removed */
    92	export function EventModel(
    93	  pointer: string | EventPointer,
    94	): Model<NostrEvent | undefined, IEventStore | IAsyncEventStore> {
    95	  if (typeof pointer === "string") pointer = { id: pointer };
    96	
    97	  return (store) =>
    98	    merge(
    99	      // get current event
   100	      defer(() => getEventFromStores(store, pointer)).pipe(
   101	        // If the event isn't found, attempt to load using the fallback loader
   102	        store.eventLoader ? loadEventUsingFallback(store, pointer) : identity,
   103	      ),
   104	      // Listen for new events
   105	      store.insert$.pipe(filter((e) => e.id === pointer.id)),
   106	      // emit undefined when deleted
   107	      store.remove$.pipe(
   108	        filter((e) => e.id === pointer.id),
   109	        // Complete when the event is removed
   110	        take(1),
   111	        // Emit undefined when deleted
   112	        map(() => undefined),
   113	      ),
   114	    ).pipe(
   115	      // ignore duplicate events (true === same)
   116	      distinctUntilChanged((a, b) => a?.id === b?.id),
   117	      // claim all events
   118	      claimLatest(store),
   119	    );
   120	}

    97	- `defer(getEventFromStores)` lazily reads the store on each subscription.
    98	- Optional fallback loader injected via `loadEventUsingFallback` (lines 73-89) that emits `undefined` first then the loaded event — important for UI: don't render stale, render loading.
    99	- Merges three streams: initial fetch, `insert$.filter(id)`, and `remove$.filter(id).map(() => undefined).take(1)`.
   100	- `distinctUntilChanged` by id, `claimLatest` to pin.
   101	
   102	### `ReplaceableModel(pointer)` — lines 123-173
   103	- Same shape but filters `insert$` by `(pubkey, kind, identifier)` (lines 137-143).
   104	- The `current` variable + `tap` at line 146 is acknowledged as hacky — it tracks the current event so the `remove$` filter can match by id (you can't know which id was current until something else updated it).
    41	### D1. Best-effort rendering — render now, refine in place
    42	
    43	Apps built with this framework **never withhold cached data and never block on fetches**. Every view payload field carries a value, not a "loading" status. Missing display names default to a shortened npub; missing pictures default to a deterministic identicon URI; missing timestamps default to "now". When a more authoritative value (e.g., the author's kind:0) arrives later, the view payload updates in place and the affected cell re-renders. The UI never sees a spinner gating already-renderable content.
    44	
    45	The doctrine is enforced by the view payload **types**: display fields are non-`Option`, placeholders are part of the type contract, and freshness is exposed (when relevant) as an optional badge hint, not a render gate. There is no `if has_profile { render } else { spinner }` pattern available in the API — the framework does not provide one.

commit 8d633e82026ab9f151854b29ab4f504b0883f7e8
Author: pablof7z <pfer@me.com>

    research(applesauce+ndk): deep-dive notes for M2 outbox + framework-magic


 succeeded in 0ms:
104:+- Optional fallback loader injected via `loadEventUsingFallback` (lines 73-89) that emits `undefined` first then the loaded event — important for UI: don't render stale, render loading.
144:+- `selectOptimalRelays` (`helpers/relay-selection.ts:14-93`) is a greedy set-cover: each iteration picks the relay covering the most uncovered users, optionally biased by `score(relay, coverage, popularity)`. `maxRelaysPerUser` caps per-user concentration. The TODO at line 89 acknowledges that the final per-user relay list may exceed `maxRelaysPerUser` because the count is enforced during selection, not after.
145:+- `OutboxModel.getKey` (`models/outbox.ts:26-29`) hashes only `[pubkey, type, maxConnections, maxRelaysPerUser]` — the blacklist and `score` function are intentionally excluded so they can be changed without forcing a new pipeline.
195:+**Commit `b03c0d96`** ("Fix timeline backwards loader not handling `until` correctly on filters"). Pre-fix: after loading a block, the next `until` was set to the oldest event's `created_at`, but NIP-01 defines `until` as **inclusive**, so the same event would be returned again at the boundary, causing an infinite loop on singleton blocks. Fix at `loaders/timeline-loader.ts:107`: `if (minCreatedAt !== undefined) cursor = minCreatedAt - 1;`.
341:+2. **`share()` with keepWarm + ReplaySubject(1) semantics.** `event-models.ts:73-78`. Every typed view subscription must dedupe across consumers, replay last value to new subscribers, and stay warm for ~60s after the last unsubscribe.
521:+3. **Re-emission on every change.** `combineLatest` re-emits on any inner change. NMP must size its planner debouncer accordingly — naive re-resolution on each kind:10002 will thrash; `OutboxModel` itself doesn't debounce, downstream consumers do via the model-cache 60s keep-warm.
539:+The TODO at line 89 acknowledges a known imprecision: `maxRelaysPerUser` is enforced during the greedy pass but not as a post-filter, so a user can end up with more than `maxRelaysPerUser` final relays if their first picks happened to cover the pool.
785:+`getRelayListForUsers` timeout fired before EOSE arrived from relays → empty relay lists → subscriptions never connecting to user relays. Fix: added `resolved` flag (prevent double-resolve), conditional timeout that extends +3s when relays are still connecting. **Implication**: outbox bootstrap is timing-sensitive; consider exposing a "wait until relay lists known" gate in NMP UX before showing follow feed.
1155:+Source explicitly notes the gap: `// TODO: The state of this tracker needs to be added to cache adapters` (`tracker.ts:48-49`).
1185:+`calculateRelaySetFromEvent` doesn't fully account for relays where specific hashtags are popular (`relay/sets/calculate.ts:18-19` TODO). For tag-heavy posts (e.g., #bitdevs), publishing is suboptimal.
1189:+`getTopRelaysForAuthors` has TODO to incorporate quality metrics. Currently ranks by author-count only.
1197:+`NDKSync.sync` / `syncAndSubscribe` are not the default path. Regular `ndk.subscribe` doesn't try negentropy. For large historical fetches (e.g., loading the last week of a 500-follow feed cold), NMP should reach for sync directly.
1435:+Outbox tracker state is *not* persisted to cache adapters — there is a `TODO` in `tracker.ts:48-49` noting rehydration is unimplemented. On every fresh app boot, the tracker is empty and the first wave of subscriptions pays full discovery cost.

 succeeded in 0ms:
   136	- `includeMailboxes` uses `combineLatest(contacts.map(user => store.replaceable({kind:10002,pubkey:user.pubkey})...))`. That means **adding one contact spawns one new inner observable that itself goes through the shared-model cache**. If the same user is already mailbox-tracked by another model, the inner observable is the same shared instance — zero extra relay traffic.
   137	- The map-projection at `relay-selection.ts:32-43` returns the original `user` pointer when the kind:10002 hasn't loaded yet; it does **not** drop the contact. That's intentional — partial outbox knowledge still resolves *something*.
   138	- `selectOptimalRelays` (`helpers/relay-selection.ts:14-93`) is a greedy set-cover: each iteration picks the relay covering the most uncovered users, optionally biased by `score(relay, coverage, popularity)`. `maxRelaysPerUser` caps per-user concentration. The TODO at line 89 acknowledges that the final per-user relay list may exceed `maxRelaysPerUser` because the count is enforced during selection, not after.
   139	- `OutboxModel.getKey` (`models/outbox.ts:26-29`) hashes only `[pubkey, type, maxConnections, maxRelaysPerUser]` — the blacklist and `score` function are intentionally excluded so they can be changed without forcing a new pipeline.
   140	
    14	export function OutboxModel(user: string | ProfilePointer, opts: OutboxModelOptions): Model<ProfilePointer[]> {
    15	  return (store) =>
    16	    store.contacts(user).pipe(
    17	      /** Ignore blacklisted relays */
    18	      opts?.blacklist ? ignoreBlacklistedRelays(opts.blacklist) : identity,
    19	      /** Include mailboxes */
    20	      includeMailboxes(store, opts.type),
    21	      /** Select the optimal relays */
    22	      map((users) => selectOptimalRelays(users, opts)),
    23	    );
    24	}
    25	
    26	OutboxModel.getKey = (user: string | ProfilePointer, opts: OutboxModelOptions) => {
    27	  const p = typeof user === "string" ? user : user.pubkey;
    28	  return hash_sum([p, opts.type, opts.maxConnections, opts.maxRelaysPerUser]);
    29	};

docs/product-spec/subsystems.md:293:### 7.9 Wallet
docs/product-spec/subsystems.md:295:`nmp-wallet` is staged. NIP-47 Wallet Connect lands first because it is a bounded client protocol over the action ledger and secret capabilities. Cashu/NIP-60 and nutzaps/NIP-61 come later because they require a durable wallet state machine, mint metadata cache, proof/token indexes, redemption state, and repair flows.

No wallet UI hook mutates proof, token, nutzap, or transaction state directly; those records live in the actor-owned domain store and transition through the action ledger.
